< Text>
Excellent quality, caring cheerful service, professional office operations.  I've been going to Riley Dental Group for about 30 years. During that time I moved to Santa Clarita, which is further away from San Fernando where Riley's office is located.  Yet I still drive to San Fernando for their outstanding dental care.

Go to Riley's once and you'll go the rest of your life.</Text>

I had only one concern really, and it is a common concern I find at many motels/hotels:  the irrigation system sprays the car overnight which leaves hard water spots which require professional cleaning and buffing to remove- - unlike rain water which is soft and leaves no permanent spots.< /Text>

< Text>
The hotel and staff are nice even though the hotel itself is under some very minor renovation right now. 
I was assigned to room #231 which is on the second floor above the lobby. It was a nice clean room, which I checked into around 6pm. When I entered the room, I turned on the TV and started to changed clothes to go to dinner around 7pm. When I got back around 8:30pm or 9pm from dinner I went up to my room and turned on the TV for an hour or more before I tried to fall asleep. This was when it all started because I kept hearing a "loud banging sound" from the outside window wall. The banging sound was so irregular when it would go off that I tried not to pay much attention because I just assumed it was coming from something outside the hotel. 
However, it woke me up again at midnight, 2am or so, at 3:30am or so and then finally at 5:30am it just kept going off continuously about every five to ten minutes. Just so you know I figured out what the noise was around midnight but I thought it would not be a problem again but was I ever wrong. (The noise was coming from the sliding doors in the lobby whenever they would move). So every time the sliding doors opened or closed that night, I heard a big bang sound and it would wake me up. I told the hotel clerk in the morning that it was a terrible night because I could not sleep because of the noise from the sliding doors and that the hotel needed to convert room #231 to a closet or something beside a hotel room for guests but I don't think the clerk really cared about my opinion because he/she did not offer me any real sympathy, except "I'm sorry."
To be honest, the clerk was a nice person but I just don't think he/she cared that the sliding doors were a huge problem to room #231 and me. Again, the hotel is nice but, "DO NOT STAY IN ROOM #231!!!!!". 
*I left the clerk hotel person without a gender because honestly the problem is not the staff at this hotel but just room #231 and the sliding doors in the lobby.</Text>

This restaurant is simply perfect!

Staff were friendly and professional, and the food was so good!
We ordered premixed cocktails and wine and sat on the street-side patio while we waited for our table. The wait wasn't long and even though it was freezing outside, they took care of that with heaters throughout the patio area (enough for me to cuddle with one haha). I wish I remembered my servers name but everyone I interacted with was amazing.

The ambiance outside was quiet, cozy and romantic. Absolutely loved it.<//review>

A friend brought me here for coffee and a pastry after morning Mass and it quite a revelation. I have passed this establishment dozens of times and frankly never knew that it has a double life â€” in the morning it is a breakfast joint and the evening is a very fancy pizza restaurant featuring a cocktail menu and dessert selections.

Since I only spent a single morning here I can only comment on the breakfast hours which was very pleasant - the coffee was robust and the cheese and chive biscuit was quite tasty. The atmosphere was cozy - there was a mix of seating options from benches or booth setups and tables and chairs to accommodate individuals, couples and groups. Kiddos were welcome. Patrons could use WiFi. It was possible to enjoy a conversation and not feel rushed. I wouldnâ€™t mind a return visit to try other menu items.<//Text>

<name>Rissa Park<//name><text>Quite pricey, but otherwise a nice experience. The atmosphere is very romantic. Dim lights, artwork, brick, warm, elegant. Very nice patio seating.
This was a genuine italian pizza location. Unless you are familiar with Italian cuisine, I suggest looking up the menu beforehand, as we were unfamiliar with a lot of the items/terms. Wood fired pizza was delicious, but expensive and light on toppings. The desserts were great. We had afogatto and the seasonal stone fruit. There seemed to be a great wine/drink menu, although we did not have any.
If you are looking for classic pepperoni pizza with tons of cheese, this may not be the place. However, if you are looking for a cultural experience, this is a great place.
Pricing wise - we had 2 pizzas, bread, and 2 desserts and spent $70. Additional pizza toppings are $5 a piece.<//text></record>

< Review>
Like others I am also extremely confused why this restaurant has a high rating, I do not in all honesty think it deserves for several reasons, food taste and service alone. Once again, the average American audience that lack knowledge of authentic food and love for imitation
When I crave Italian I avoid going to restaurants whose chefs and staff are not from Italy, because I am aware it is extremely difficult to get it right. Lucia's in Berkeley downtown does a better job.

I visited Sunday evening around 7 PM, hoping for an authentic Italian cuisine. We started by visiting the female host who showed up a cramped up table for two, we then requested she take us to a spacious table, as a preference. She threw her subtle grumpy attitude towards this and was annoyed on our request, wherein in practice she should not want to give such reactions and be happy that the guest came in. However, staff don't care because they just want to get paid their salary and go home, it's NOT their business so why care, let's be grumpy.
Then after being seated, no one came to use for 15-20 minutes, leaving us completely ignored. I had to ask a guy walking around to serve me some water. Another horrible attitude for an above average priced restaurant. Upon asking the same guy to get my order, then came my server after 5 minutes. I asked her if there were any options on the menu with no meat Pizza and she plainly said "Whatever's on the menu." I do not think she wanted to work that day. I then told her that I do not understand the ingredients so would like her to help me point at some options, and again the non-gratuitous attitude followed. I ordered one of the Pizza and it came, to my mind, very distasteful. It was an Americanized version of imitative Italian Pizza and I was not interested in that. Sorry.

I am surprised that one of the co-owners is from Italy, she definitely has not paid attention to the operations, in my opinion. Sorry for being blunt.</Review>

<user_id>117686719924044235401</user_id>< text>
I've eaten here a few times over the years, and it's been up and down, with some memorably bad experiences when they first opened. After a long hiatus, we were persuaded to return for dinner, and sadly, it's a place to skip.

We 3 shared a marguerita di buffala pizza, the meatballs, a little gem salad, and fried chicken with potatoes au gratin, plus dessert. I'll address them one at a time :
the pizza, pleasant enough, but at $20, for a very small pizza, a little dear. Plus no basil in evidence, and instead of being sliced it appeared to have been merely lightly scored, which made eating it unnecessarily awkward.
the salad - delicious baby romaine and roasted beets, but quite a tiny portion, and again, $14 too dear.
the meatballs - not very good. flavor just meh. we make much better meatballs at home. and somewhat misleadingly, as it is listed amongst the primi with 2 other pasta dishes, this is NOT served with any pasta. there is a nice slice of grilled bread, but not quite what one might expect.
fried chicken - very good, tender, moist and tasty, but again overpriced. $29 for only one breast? surely for a secondi and at that price, they should serve a breast and a leg, or a half chicken. The most upsetting part was the potatoes au gratin, which were exceedingly undercooked, almost crunchy.

service was fine. we were probably not their target market, as we were placed in a back room away from most of the diners - and all of the heat. it was really too cold back there, and had i known the front of the house was nice and toasty, i would have asked to be moved.

Dessert was tasty enough, but portions! Really? Panna cotta tasted lovely, but i swear we were served max 4 tablespoons for $12. Honey cake was ok - same price, and rather dry.

So, we will not return. And i'd suggest you look elsewhere too.<//text>

<user>101995889170262487972<//user>< Text>
Depending on where you sit in the restaurant, the atmosphere lends itself to date night, family time, girls night out, as well as celebrations in the semi-private room for parties of about 20ppl or less. The menu is seasonal and changes daily with almost everything made in house using fresh, local ingredients. Right now shell beans and tomatoes are on the menu and it's so good! Just a suggestion but I would get the housemade bread (Acme on mondays) which has a crunchy outside crust and a soft, doughy center to sop up all that yummy tomatoey goodness at the bottom of your plate. In terms of drinks, the housemade tonic is a must! Bourbon is my preference, but whatever you decide will work too. Also, remember to Leave Room For Dessert! Trust me, you won't be disappointed.</Text>

Best Italian food so far in East bay< /Text>

1466971821434< /date>

< review>
Dinner here on 25 June 2016 was a decidedly unimpressive experience in almost all regards.

We (two) arrived without a reservation, left our name, and were asked to return in 15 minutes, which we did.  At that point, we were seated immediately - at the same table, within arm's reach of the reservations podium, that had been empty when we first arrived.

We ordered a pizza (listed as having rapini and homemade sausage) and polenta with gorgonzola.  They were served simultaneously, as we had requested.

The polenta was tasty, although lacking any aesthetic with its single piece of gorgonzola chunked into the polenta.

The pizza arrived with significant portions of the rim burned to blackness.  It was nice to know that it was apparently done in a wood-fired oven, but with the well-recognized health dangers of eating charred food, it hardly seems a wise choice to serve.  (We happened to notice that the pizza at our neighbor's table was even worse in this regard, with nearly the entire rim looking like the remnants of a house fire...)

The sausage on the pizza was overpoweringly salty.  The rapini was cooked to an appropriate level and brought a nice flavor.  A big surprise was that there were nearly as many purple onions as there were sausage or rapini.  It seemed odd that they should be unlisted on the menu description.

Service by our waitress was competent and efficient.  The person who brought water, removed dishes, etc., did his job without a single word of announcement or acknowledgment - he just plunked things on the table where he thought they should go, took away items he presumably thought were no longer needed, etc.

In brief - there was little that was pleasant and nothing that was beyond expectations, while a fair number of elements failed to meet what we consider reasonable, basic standards.  For us, this trip to Pizzaiolo will almost certainly be "one and done).<//review>
